# Tundra Compendium

Tundras are vast, cold, and often desolate landscapes that present unique challenges and opportunities for adventurers. These harsh environments serve as significant barriers to travel, testing the endurance and resilience of those who dare to cross them. Tundras can be the setting for dour quests, where survival against the elements is as much a part of the adventure as any enemy or dungeon. These bleak and unforgiving landscapes provide a grim and foreboding backdrop for any adventure.

\columnbreak


This document provides content to help you run games that feature tundras of various types, from the icy plains of the far north to temperate regions plunged into harsh winters. This content ranges from character options for players who want their characters to be associated with winter or tundra regions, to mechanics for running sessions with travel through tundras to a bestiary of tundra creatures to populate the icy regions of your games. Whether the players are only spending a day traveling through the cold or your entire campaign takes place in the arctic, any of the content here can be used to enhance your games.

## Tundra Adventure Ideas

Tundra and winter environments make for natural adventure locales. The following adventure hooks can be used as inspiration for creating your own icy adventures. They could either be minor side quests or part of much larger campaign-spanning adventures.

##### Tundra Adventure Hooks

| d8  | Setup |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Tundra Beast:** Rumors of a gigantic beast terrorizing isolated villages on the tundra reach the adventurers. Tasked with stopping the creature, they discover it is actually a cursed druid. |
|  2  | 	T**he Frozen Heart:** A powerful artifact known as the Frozen Heart has been stolen, plunging the region into an eternal winter. The adventurers are hired to retrieve the artifact and restore balance to the climate. |
|  3  | **Icebound Expedition:** An expedition team searching for a lost city of ice has gone missing. The adventurers are hired to find the team and explore the secrets of the lost city. |

##### Tundra Adventure Ideas Art Credit

* Winter Wolves - Robson Michel, Wizards of the Coast

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

|   |  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  4  | **Frozen Shipwreck:** An ancient ship has been found frozen in the ice, its crew preserved in time. The adventurers must investigate the ship, uncover its history, and deal with any dangers that still linger. The ship holds valuable cargo and secrets of a lost civilization, but its former crew may not be as dead as they appear. |
|  5  | **Winter's Wrath:** A powerful winter spirit has cursed a region with unending blizzards. The adventurers must appease the spirit or break its curse to bring back the warmth of spring. |
|  6  | **Frozen Refuge:** Refugees from a neighboring kingdom seek shelter in the tundra after their homeland is invaded. The adventurers must escort them to safety, navigating the harsh terrain and avoiding pursuers.  |
|  7  | **The Glacial Crypt:** A glacier has receded to reveal the entrance to an ancient crypt. The adventurers are hired to explore the crypt and retrieve any magical artifacts within, facing undead guardians and treacherous traps. |
|  8  | 	**Winter Wolf Raiders:** A group of marauding winter wolves has been raiding supply caravans, leaving the survivors to face the harsh elements without resources. The adventurers are tasked with protecting the next caravan and tracking the wolves to their lair, where they must face the pack in a brutal showdown. |

<br>

# Player <br> Options

## Druid Circle

### Circle of The Tundra
Most druids of this circle make their homes in the coldest environments their world has to offer, and they have adapted all aspects of their druidic abilities to reflect this harsh environment.  They practice shapeshifting into arctic creatures while channeling the brutal nature of their boreal homes to unleash icy magics upon their enemies and can even summon and control enchanted glaciers with which to smite their foes.

#### Tundra Spells
*2nd Level Circle of the Tundra Feature*<br>
Your mystical connection to the arctic infuses you with the ability to cast certain spells.  Once you gain access to one of these spells, you always have it prepared, and it doesn't count against the number of spells you can prepare each day.  If you gain access to a spell that doesn't appear on the druid spell list, the spell is nonetheless a druid spell for you.  

##### Circle of The Tundra Spells

| Druid  Level  |  Spells      | 
|:-------------:|:-------------:|
|  2nd          | *armor of agathys*, *ice knife* |
|  3rd          | *ice sheet**, *frost nova** |
|  5th          | *sleet storm*, *winter's kiss**   | 
|  7th          | *fire shield*(cold shield only), *ice storm** |
|  9th          | *cone of cold*, *icy tomb** |

**New spell found in New Spells section*

#### Tundra Forms
*2nd Level Circle of The Tundra Feature* <br>
You can now use your Wild Shape feature to transform into unique arctic animal forms granted by this subclass, and when using your Wild Shape this way, you may use it as a bonus action. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br>

Detailed descriptions of these forms can be found in the Tundra Wild Shapes section.

When shapeshifting into these forms, you can choose to either be Small or Medium. Starting at 10th level, you can also choose to be Large. 

While in these forms, you can perform the somatic and verbal components of druid spells from your Tundra Spells list and ignore their material component requirements.

You start knowing three of these forms: Elk, Wolf, and Wolverine. Additional wild shape forms from this subclass become available at levels 4 and 8. (In the case of the Elephant and Rhino forms, you become wooly versions of these creatures.)

##### Tundra Wild Shape Options
| Druid  Level  |  Wild Shape Option      | 
|:-------------:|:-------------:|
|  2nd          | Elk, Wolf, Wolverine |
|  4th          | Bear, Leopard Seal, Lynx | 
|  8th          | Elephant, Rhino|

#### Boreal Dweller
*2nd Level Circle of The Tundra Feature*<br>
You gain resistance to cold damage. If you already have resistance to cold damage from a racial feature, you instead gain advantage on Constitution saving throws against effects that would deal cold damage to you. Your movement is also unaffected by difficult terrain made of ice or snow, and such terrain can't cause you to fall prone.

Additionally, you gain an advantage on Wisdom (Survival) and Intelligence (Nature) checks relating to tundra environments and the life that inhabits them. You can also speak with animals who dwell in tundra environments as though under the effects of the *speak with animals* spell, and you have advantage on Wisdom (Animal Handling) checks made while interacting with them.



<img src='https://i.ibb.co/X5YYM13/Moritte-of-the-Frost.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-150px; right:-60px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(0deg)scalex(-1);filter:opacity(100%);'/>

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-140px;top:-42px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(194deg)' />






\pagebreakNum

#### Primal Weapons
*6th Level Circle of The Tundra feature* <br>
If you merge into any of your wild shapes with a magical weapon you are wielding, your attacks in that wild shape count as magical for the purpose of overcoming resistance and immunity to nonmagical attacks and damage.

#### Glacial Summoning
*6th Level Circle of The Tundra Feature*<br>
You've gained the ability to call forth icy manifestations of your boreal homelands.  You may use your action to summon a glacial mass of ice, causing it to burst from a location on the ground or on top of a liquid surface that you can see within 20 feet.  The ice can be up to 10 feet long on any side, and it must be summoned in an unoccupied space large enough to contain it.

The ice has an AC 14 and hit points equal to five times your druid level.  It is immune to poison, psychic, cold damage, and vulnerable to fire, thunder and bludgeoning damage.  If reduced to 0 hit points, it crumbles to mist.

The ice emanates a 10-foot aura of cold, and creatures other than you treat the space in this aura as difficult terrain.

As a bonus action, you can move the ice up to 20 feet along any solid or liquid surface.  If you move the ice into a creature, that creature must make the Dexterity saving throw against your spell save DC.  The creature takes 3d8 cold damage on a failed save, or half as much on a successful one.

Once you summon the glacial, you cannot summon one again until you complete a long rest or until you expend a spell slot of 3rd level or higher.



\columnbreak

#### Avatar of The Tundra
*10th Level Circle of Tundra feature* <br>
When you use your Wild Shape feature to transform into one of the forms granted by this subclass, you can choose one of the following enhancements while in that form:

* **Aurora Form.** Your form is infused with the shimmering lights of the polar night sky, causing you to glow with a dancing green radiance. You emit bright light in a 30-foot radius and dim light for an additional 30 feet. Additionally, you have a fly speed equal to your form's walking speed.

* **Primordial Form.** Your form grows to the immense size of ancient megafauna. Your size becomes Huge in your new form, and your melee weapon attacks deal an extra 1d4 damage. Additionally, you get a +2 bonus to Strength saving throws and the spell save DC for any abilities your wild shape has.

* **Wendigo Form.** Your form becomes emaciated and sinuous as you hunger for the warmth of life. When you hit a non-undead, non-construct creature with a melee attack granted by your wild shape, you regain hit points equal to half the amount of damage dealt.


#### Frozen Assault
*14th Level Circle of The Tundra Feature*<br>
You can now channel the remorseless fury of the north through your attacks. Whenever you would deal bludgeoning, piercing, or slashing damage with a melee weapon attack, you may change the damage type to cold.
 
Additionally, whenever you deal cold damage to a creature or a creature starts its turn in an area of difficult terrain composed of ice or snow created by one of your druid spells or features, you may reduce its speed by 10 feet until the end of your next turn. This speed reduction can't stack multiple times on a single creature. 

 <img src='https://i.ibb.co/LgCk53C/Snow-Covered-Plains-Secret-Lair-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:555px; right:00px; width:850px; transform: scaleX(-1)' />

## Tundra <br> Wild Shapes
The following stat blocks are <br> listed in alphabetical order and <br> describe the new wild shape <br> options granted by the Circle of <br>  the Tundra subclass.

___
> ## Bear Shape
> *Small, Medium, or Large (must be 10th level druid or higher to be Large) (your
creature type doesn’t change), unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 11 + your Wisdom modifier
> - **Hit Points** 8 + 4 times your level in this class
> - **Speed** 40 ft., climb 25 ft., swim 25 ft
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|Equals your Wisdom score| Equals your Wisdom score|Equals your Wisdom score|Equals your score |Equals your score|Equals your score|
>___
> - **Senses** darkvision 30 ft.
> - **Languages** the languages you know
> - **Proficiency Bonus** equals your bonus
> ___
>
> ***Burly.*** You have advantage on Strength and Constitution checks and saving throws.
>
> ***Keen Hearing and Smell.*** You have advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell or hearing.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack (requires you to be a 6th level druid or higher).*** You make a Bite and a Claw attack.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Attack:* your Spell Attack Modifier
to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 1d8 + your Wisdom modifier piercing damage
>
> ***Claw.*** *Melee Attack:* your Spell Attack Modifier
to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 1d10 + your Wisdom modifier slashing damage.

___
___
> ## Elephant Shape
> *Small, Medium, or Large (must be 10th level druid or higher to be Large) (your
creature type doesn’t change), unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 12 + your Wisdom modifier
> - **Hit Points** 8 + 4 times your level in this class
> - **Speed** 35 ft.,
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|Equals your Wisdom score| Equals your Wisdom score|Equals your Wisdom score|Equals your score |Equals your score|Equals your score|
>___
> - **Languages** the languages you know
> - **Proficiency Bonus** Equals your Proficiency Bonus
> ___
>
> ***Brawn.*** You have advantage on Strength checks and saving throws.
>
> ***Charge.*** If you move at least 20 ft. straight toward a target and then hit it with a Gore attack on the same turn, the target must succeed on a Strength saving throw against your spell save DC or be knocked prone.
>
> ***Keen Hearing.*** You have advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on hearing.
>
> ***Trunk.*** You can grasp objects with your trunk and use it as a snorkel. Your trunk has a reach of 10ft. and can lift up objects weighing a number of pounds up to 30 times your Wisdom score. Your trunk can be used to perform the following simple tasks: lift, drop, hold, push, or pull an object or a creature; open or close a door or container.
> 
> It can't wield weapons or shields or do anything that requires manual precision, such as using tools, magic items, or performing the somatic components of a spell.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** You make a Gore and Stomp attack and a Trunk Grab or Fling. 
>
> ***Gore.*** *Melee Attack:* your Spell Attack Modifier
to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 1d8 + your Wisdom modifier piercing damage.
>
> ***Stomp.*** *Melee Attack:* your Spell Attack Modifier
to hit, reach 5 ft., one prone target. *Hit:* 1d12 + your Wisdom modifier bludgeoning damage.
>
> ***Trunk Grab.*** *Melee Attack:* your Spell Attack Modifier
to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* The target is grappled by your trunk.
>
> ***Fling.*** You choose one object or creature you are holding or grappling with your trunk that is your size or smaller and throw it up to 20 feet away. If the target hits a solid surface, it takes 1d6 + your Wisdom modifier damage and lands prone. If the thrown target would hit another creature, the creature that would be hit must make a Dexterity saving against your spell save DC. On a failed save, the creature is hit, takes 1d6 + your Wisdom modifier bludgeoning damage, and is knocked prone. On a successful save, it dodges out of the way, takes no damage, and is not knocked prone.
>

## New Spells: <bR> Lore of Ice
This brand of magic draws on the powers of the frigid <br> north and winter itself. Those who practice it often dwell <br> in tundra locals, but others may revere winter and its solstice. Still, others may simply be elemental enthusiasts looking to compliment their magical arsenal with some freezing spells. Most of these spells conjure icey phenomena or unleash blasts of freezing magic capable of encasing targets in ice. The following spells are examples of the types of magic users of the Lore of Ice often wield.

#### Deathly Frost
*5th-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 90 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard.

You cause a creature to be gripped by freezing cold. Until the spell ends, at the end of each of your turns, if the target is within 90 feet of you, it must make Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, it takes 5d8 cold damage and suffers one level of exhaustion. On a successful save, the creature takes half as much damage and does not suffer a level of exhaustion. A creature immune to cold damage can't gain exhaustion this way. Any levels of exhaustion caused by this spell go away after the spell ends.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

#### Frost Blade
*3rd-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Artificer, Druid, Ranger, Sorcerer

You invoke a sword of sharp ice in your hand or that of another willing creature you can see within range that has a free hand. This magic sword lasts until the spell ends. 

**The Blade's Properties.** It counts as a magical, simple melee weapon with which you and any number of creatures of your choice upon casting the spell are proficient with. It deals 2d10 slashing damage on hit and has the finesse, versatile (2d12), and thrown (range 60/90) properties. 

**Throwing The Blade.** When a creature uses the sword to make a thrown attack, hit or miss, the weapon explodes, and the spell ends. The target and each creature within 10 feet of it must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or take 4d6 cold damage.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 5th level or higher, you may create an additional sword for every two levels above 3rd level.


<img src='https://i.ibb.co/D7x78wT/Chill-to-the-Bone-1200x.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-130px; right:-80px; width:900px;' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-110px;top:175px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(195deg)' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-110px;top:260px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(180deg)' />



\pagebreakNum

#### Frost Nova
*2nd-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Self (15-foot radius)
- **Components:** V, S, M (a drop of water <br> or piece of ice)
- **Duration:**   Instantaneous
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard
___

You cause a ring of ice and frost to burst out from you to a radius of up to a 15-feet. Each creature other than you in that area must make a Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 2d10 cold damage, and until the end of your next turn, its speed is reduced by 20 feet, and it has disadvantage on weapon attack rolls. On a successful save, a creature takes half as much damage and suffers no other effects.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, both the damage increases by 1d10, and the maximum possible radius increases by 5 feet for each slot level above 3rd.


\columnbreak

#### Ice Sheet 
*2nd-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 Action
- **Range:** 30 feet
- **Components:** S, M (a drop of water or piece of ice)
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Druid
___

A wave of cold 30 feet long and 15 feet wide emanates from you in a direction you choose. The ground in the area is covered with ice, turning it into difficult terrain for the duration. Any surface of a body of water or a liquid that is principally water-based within the area freezes to a depth of 6 inches for the duration. Creatures may move across the frozen surfaces as if they are difficult terrain. 

**Destroying The Ice.** A 5-foot square area of ice can be destroyed by attacking it (AC equal to your spell save; HP 20; vulnerability to fire, thunder bludgeoning damage; immunity to cold, poison, and psychic damage). 

**Slipping On The Ice.** When the ice appears, each creature standing in its area must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or fall prone. A creature that enters the area or ends its turn there must also succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or fall prone. 

**Being Caught In The Water.** If a creature is swimming in an area where ice appears, it must make a Strength saving throw instead or become restrained by ice for the duration. A creature restrained by the ice or another creature that can reach it can also use its action to make a Strength check against your spell save DC. On a success, the target is freed. The target is also freed if any ice where at its location is destroyed. On a successful save, the creature can move below or above the now frozen surface.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 3rd level or higher, the length of the line increases by 10 feet for each slot level above 2nd.

#### Ice Storm 
*4th-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 300 feet
- **Components:** V, S, M (a pinch of dust and a few <br> drops of water)
- **Duration:**  1 Round
- **Classes:**  Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard
___

A barrage of rock-hard ice plummets from the sky, forming a 20-foot-radius, 40-foot-high cylinder centered on a point within range. The area becomes difficult terrain until the end of your next turn, and any  creature within it has disadvantage on ranged attack rolls.

When the ice storm initially appears or if a creature is inside its area at the end of your next turn, the creature must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, it takes 3d4 bludgeoning damage and 3d4 cold damage. On a successful save, it takes half as much damage.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 5th level or higher, both the bludgeoning and cold damage increase by 1d4 for each slot level above 4th.

src='https://i.ibb.co/qYHnBcs/icy-blast.png'
style='position:absolute;bottom:-5px;right:200px;width:870px;transform: scaleX(-1)' />

#### Icy Tomb
*5th-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 reaction, which you take when you or a creature you can see within range would take damage or make a death saving throw.
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:**   Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Druid, Sorcerer, Warlock, Wizard

Ice encases one willing Medium or smaller creature you can see within range. It is trapped inside a Medium-sized ice block object that occupies its space for the duration of the spell or until the ice is reduced to 0 hit points. The ice has an AC equal to your spell save; HP 50; vulnerability to fire, thunder bludgeoning damage; immunity to cold, poison, and psychic damage). A creature trapped inside the ice is blinded, restrained, incapacitated, has total cover against attacks and other effects outside the ice, and becomes stable if it is at 0 hit points.

**Casting It As An Action.** You can choose to cast this spell as an action on your turn, choosing any creature within range. If the creature is not willing, it may make a Strength saving throw; on success, the spell ends and has no effect on the creature.

**Damaging The Ice From Within.** A creature inside the ice can choose to deal bludgeoning damage to the ice equal to 1d6 + its Strength modifier at the end of each of its turns.

**Casting It On Yourself.** If you cast the spell on yourself, it does not require Concentration, and you can choose to end the spell at the start of your turn. 

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 6th level or higher, the ice block gains 10 additional Hit Points for each slot level above 5th.



#### Snowball Swarm 
*2nd-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** Self
- **Components:** V, S, M (a piece of ice or a small white rock chip)
- **Duration:** Up to 10 minutes
- **Classes:** Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard
___

You summon a flurry of magic snowballs to bombard your enemies. When you cast the spell, you may make two ranged spell attacks with the snowballs against any targets within 90 feet of you. On a hit, a target takes cold damage equal to 1d4 + your spellcasting ability modifier. During the spell's duration, you can use an action to form two more snowballs and make the attacks again.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, you may make one additional snowball attack per action for every two slot levels above 2nd.

<img src='https://cards.scryfall.io/art_crop/front/d/9/d99a4bbc-660f-442b-9300-69c4141348f6.jpg?1672377338' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; right:-500px; width:1447px;' />

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/BKKrNrc/Freeze-in-Place-Wilds-of-Eldraine-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; right:-125px; width:1460px;' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png'

#### Soul of Winter
*9th-level conjuration*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 action
- **Range:** 120 ft
- **Components:** V, S, M (sapphire worth 100 gp)
- **Duration:** Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard

A 30-foot-radius sphere of whirling sub-zero cold springs into existence centered on a point you choose within range. The sphere remains for the spell's duration. 

**Creatures In the Sphere When It's First Cast.** Each creature in the sphere, when it first appears, must succeed on a Strength saving. On a failed save, a creature takes 5d8 cold damage and is restrained by ice for 1 minute. It or another creature within reach of it can use its action to make a Strength check against your spell save, shattering the ice on a success. The ice can also be attacked and destroyed (AC equal to your spell save; HP 20; vulnerability to fire, thunder bludgeoning damage; immunity to cold, poison, and psychic damage). On a successful save, a creature takes half as much damage and isn't restrained.

**Icy Surfaces.** The surfaces within the sphere are coated in ice, making any ground in the area difficult terrain for one minute. The first time each turn that a creature either moves into or out of any difficult terrain created by the spell, it must make a Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, it falls prone. 

**Creatures Ending Their Turn In The Sphere.** Any creature that ends its turn in the area must succeed on a Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, it takes 5d8 cold damage and suffers one level of exhaustion. On a successful save, it takes half as much damage and does not suffer a level of exhaustion. A creature immune to cold damage can't gain exhaustion this way.

**The Spell's End.** When the spell ends, either because your concentration is broken or because you decide to end it, the ice in the sphere shatters in an explosion. Each creature in the sphere must make a Dexterity saving throw. A creature takes piercing damage equal to the total accumulated damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on <br> a successful one. The spell's base damage is 2d8. <br> At the end of each of your subsequent turns after <br> the spell has been cast, if the sphere has not yet <br> exploded, the damage increases by 2d8.





\columnbreak

#### Winter's Kiss
*3rd-level evocation*
___
- **Casting Time:** 1 bonus action
- **Range:** 60 feet
- **Components:** V, S
- **Duration:**  Concentration, up to 1 minute
- **Classes:**  Sorcerer, Wizard

A burst of cold energy emanates from you in a 40-foot cone. Each creature in that area must make a Strength saving throw. 

On a failed save, a creature takes 4d6 cold damage and is restrained by ice until the spell ends. At the end of each of its turns, while restrained this way, the target takes 2d6 cold damage. It or another creature within reach of it can use its action to make a Strength check against your spell save, shattering the ice on a success. The ice can also be attacked and destroyed (AC equal to your spell save; HP 20; vulnerability to fire, thunder bludgeoning damage; immunity to cold, poison, and psychic damage). On a successful save, a creature takes half as much damage and isn't restrained.

***At Higher Levels.*** When you cast this spell using a spell slot of 4th level or higher, the initial damage and the damage at the end of the restrained target's turn are increased by 1d6 for each slot level above 3rd.

# Tundra Travel
Tundras are among the most extreme and unforgiving environments for overland travel. They are usually sparsely inhabited, and what few paths they have are often subjected to deadly hazards. Their lack of resources and extreme cold force travelers to bring their own food and cold resistance shelters and clothing. Those who become lost in such environments are seldom heard from again, their resources quickly dwindling as they are left at the mercy of the murderous cold. 

Extreme winters can impose many of these same hazards in non-tundra environments. However, some hazards and peculiarities, such as glacial crevasses and round-the-clock nights, are only found in polar environments.

## Travel Activities
When the players travel long distances overland, tundra environments can be a significant challenge in their journey. You may modify the overland travel activities detailed in the *Player's Handbook* in the following ways when the players travel through such terrain.

### Travel Pace
If the players are traveling through deep snow or across icy terrain, it is considered rough terrain unless they have footwear that helps them cross such terrain (snow shoes, ice boots, skis, etc.) Most normal mounts and vehicles will also have trouble moving through snowy terrain, and the players may need to use vehicles such as dog sleds.

### Navigation
The difficulty in navigating tundra environments can vary greatly. The DMG suggests a navigation DC of around 10 for most arctic environments. However, expansive, featureless snowscapes would likely have a DC of 15. 

\columnbreak


<br><br><br><br><br>

If most of the environment's land features are defined by snow banks, high winds and precipitation can cause major shifts in the landscape, distorting any prior familiarity the players have with an area.

Even if the players are following a normally navigable path that would normally negate the need for navigation, snow drifts could make such paths impassible, forcing them to find alternative routes.

Depending on the cosmology and day/night mechanics of your setting, the players may also experience days or nights that are of extreme length depending on the time of year. Long or perpetual days could allow them to travel in bright light for longer, or the polar night could make navigation and spotting hazards more difficult. 



### Foraging
Tundra environments tend to have little to no natural resources. In areas too cold to support forests, the foraging DC should be 20 or higher. In forested areas, it may be 15.


### Taking Shelter
While any environment can pose challenges to travelers looking to make shelter for the night, tundras are particularly unforgiving to the unprepared. Normal tents and bedrolls may be insufficient to ward off the effects of extreme weather and cold, thus preventing them from gaining the benefits of a long rest. The players may need special cold-weather camping equipment if they can't find a natural shelter from the elements.

## Tundra Hazards
Tundras are among the most hazardous natural environments. Extreme cold, strong wind, heavy precipitation, frigid waters, thin ice, and slippery ice are all common tundra hazards described in the DMG (pg. 110). Other hazards include hidden crevasses and frigid winds.  

### Hidden Crevasses
Snowy environments can hide crevasses and sudden drops. This is especially common if the players are traveling across glacial expanses. Such drops are functionally similar to hidden pit traps. To randomly determine their depth, you can make them 1d12*20ft. deep for the typical crevasse.

#### Spotting Crevasses
Rather than using passive Perception to spot hidden crevasses, you may opt to use the passive Survival of any characters keeping a lookout. The DC to spot the fall can be anywhere from 10 (barely hidden crevasses) to 30 (supernaturally hidden crevasses). You can pick what's appropriate for your environment or roll to determine one randomly.

#### Falling Through
If a creature doesn't spot the crevasse and falls through, it can make a Dexterity save to try to catch a ledge and prevent the fall. The DC of this save depends on the nature of the fall. A relatively narrow crevasse may only have a DC 10. A large crevasse that's 10s of feed wide with supernaturally slick ice ledges may have a DC 30. This save DC can be independent of the DC to spot the fall, and you can pick one you feel is appropriate to the situation or roll to determine it randomly.

If a creature fails to grab a ledge, it falls the full length of the crevasse. 

### Winds
Rules for strong winds are described on page 110 of the DMG. If you wish to make your winds particularly hazardous, you can modify them in the following ways; the save DCs and severity of the effects these winds have are determined by the Wind Severity table.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

##### Extreme Cold
This wind carries a chill that cuts to the core. For every 1 minute a creature without cold resistance spends in the wind, it must make a Constitution save. On a failure, the creature takes an amount of cold damage dependent on the severity of the cold, and on a pass, it takes half as much damage. Creatures with insulating fur or clothing have advantage on this save.

##### Sudden Gusts
This wind will unexpectedly pick up gusts capable of bowling over creatures. At the start of every round of combat with this wind, roll 1d6. On a result of 5 or 6, all creatures not behind at least half cover are subjected to the effects of the *gust of wind* spell, except the distance they are moved on a failed save is dependent on the severity of the wind. 

If the players aren't in combat, this wind will greatly hamper travel for those not behind cover and make traveling near crevasses very dangerous. If players are traveling for an extended period of time through an open area subjected to sudden gusts, have each of them make a Strength save for each hour of travel. On a success, they are able to push through the winds, and on a failure, they treat the terrain areas as though it's rough terrain while they struggle to fight against the winds. If the terrain is already rough terrain, creatures can only move through it at 1/4th the speed. 

##### Wind Severity
|      Wind Severity      | Wind Save DC |  Cold Damage |  Gust Push Distance | 
|:--------------------:|:--------------------:|:--------------------:|:--------------------:|
|           Mild         |         10      |        1d8          |         5ft.          | 
|           Moderate         |         15         |          2d8          |         5ft.          | 
|           Intense         |         20         |           4d8    |        10ft.          | 
|           Extreme         |         25          |        6d8          |         10ft.          |
|           Supernatural         |         30         |        8d8         |         15ft.          |

## Example Random Encounter Tables
The following are different tundra environments across varying levels of gameplay, complete with random encounter tables you can use when the players are traversing them.  You can plug these right into your games, modify them to better suit your campaign, or simply use them as inspiration for creating and running your own river encounters.

Each tundra has a DC determining its foraging difficulty and an activity level suggesting how often to roll for a random encounter. There is also some information on the types of weather events likely to happen in these environments and what their DC range should be.

Not every encounter is meant to be a fight the players should be forced into. If the players are on the lower end of the level range, some of the encounters might be overwhelming for them, and they should have the option to attempt to avoid combat through other interactions, hiding, or fleeing. You can avoid encounters that seem like they wouldn't fit the current situation or modify them as needed.

Creatures on the tables with a single asterisk by their name are new creatures that can be found later in the creatures section of this document. Creatures with two asterisks can be found as free content on our website (www.StarsailGames.com) or Patreon (www.patreon.com/starsailgames). Creatures with three asterisks can be found just after the table.

### Ice Pine Tundra (Level 1-4)
**Activity Level:** 1 Encounter per 4 Hrs. of Travel <br>
**Foraging DC:** 15 <br>
**Navigation DC:** 15 <br>
**Weather DC:**  Save DCs for weather events range from 10-15.


The Ice Pine Tundra is a boreal region characterized by vast pine forests punctuated by open snow-covered hills. Recently, it has become a focal point for mystic turmoil as three renegade crone apprentices fled their mentors to test their powers. Seeking to bind fey creatures to their will, they summoned kallikantzaroi from the fey wild. However, these creatures have proven uncontrollable, wreaking havoc across the tundra. Their unchecked rampage has led to widespread deforestation, disrupting the ecosystem and driving native wildlife to exhibit erratic behavior. The once serene landscape now bears the scars of magical folly, with chaos reigning in the wake of the renegades' failed experiment.

\columnbreak

|:---:|:-------------:|

|14-15|A falling net trap in a tree with interesting carvings set by kallikantzaroi (DC 15 Passive Perception to notice it). 1d4 **kallikantzaroi*** appear 1d4 rounds after the net drops.|
|16-20|1d8 + 1 **caribou***|
|21-24|1d4 + 2 **giant owls**#|

|29-32|1 **moose***|

|55-60|1d4+1 **kallikantzaroi*** & a **kallikantzaros foreman*** being chased by a **brown bear***|

### The Winter Cursed Vale <Br>(Level 5-10)
**Activity Level:** 1 Encounter per 3 Hrs. of Travel <br>
**Foraging DC:** 10 <br>
**Navigation DC:** 10 <br>
**Weather:** Save DCs for weather events range from 15-20.

The Winter Cursed Vale was once a flourishing valley, teeming with life and home to a vibrant fiefdom. However, it has now fallen victim to a relentless curse, shrouding it in perpetual winter. This curse has not only frozen the landscape but has also awakened the dead, turning the valley into a haunting ground for roaming undead. Traveling in and out of the valley has become perilous, with the living inhabitants locked in a constant struggle for survival against the undead threats.

Adding to the chaos are hill giants from the surrounding areas, exploiting the valley's vulnerability by leading bands of ogres to pillage its remaining resources. The true origins of the curse and any potential involvement of the ruling nobility remain shrouded in mystery, adding to the sense of despair and danger that pervades the Winter Cursed Vale.

### The Far Glaciers (Level 11-16)
**Activity Level:** 1 Encounter per 6 Hrs. of Travel <br>
**Foraging DC:** 25 <br>
**Navigation DC:** 25 <br>
**Weather:** Save DCs for weather events range from 20-25.

The Far Glaciers form a remote and frigid sea, encompassing a distant archipelago devoid of settlements and rarely visited. Harsh conditions make life scarce even for animals, rendering these islands inhospitable. While thick ice blankets much of the archipelago, scholars speculate that these lands were once inhabited by an ancient civilization. Sparse artifacts hint at this, although few who venture there return to corroborate theories.

Exploring the glaciers is perilous; the bone-chilling cold and glacial dangers claim many lives. Survivors speak of forgotten horrors entombed within the ice and arcane constructs powered by unknown technologies. Such accounts are dismissed as the ramblings of madness, attributed to the extreme isolation and conditions faced in these icy depths.

##### The Far Glaciers Encounters

|:---:|:-------------:|

|14-15|Size 4 Falling Debris From a Glacier|

> ## Gibbering Monstrosity
>*Large aberration, neutral*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 12 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points**  133 (14d10 + 56)
> - **Speed** 20 ft., swim 20 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|14 (+2)|8 (-1)|18 (+4)|3 (-4)|10 (+0)|6 (-2)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Int -1, Cha +1
> - **Condition Immunities** prone
> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10
> - **Languages** ━
> - **Challenge** 5 (450 XP) &emsp;&emsp;    **Proficiency Bonus** +3
> ___
>
> ***Aberrant Ground.*** The ground in a 15-foot radius around the mouther is doughlike difficult terrain. Each creature that starts its turn in that area must succeed on a DC 13 Strength saving throw or have its speed reduced to 0 until the start of its next turn.
>
> ***Gibbering.*** The mouther babbles incoherently while it can see any creature and isn’t incapacitated. Each creature that starts its turn within 30 feet of the mouther and can hear the gibbering must succeed on a DC 11 Wisdom saving throw. On a failure, the creature can’t take reactions until the start of its next turn and rolls a d8 to determine what it does during its turn. On a 1 to 4, the creature does nothing. On a 5 or 6, the creature takes no action or bonus action and uses all its movement to move in a randomly determined direction. On a 7 or 8, the creature makes a melee attack against a randomly determined creature within its reach or does nothing if it can’t make such an attack.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The gibbering mouther makes a bite attack and, if it can, uses its Blinding Spittle.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, reach 10 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 31 (7d8) piercing damage. If the target is large or smaller, it must succeed on a DC 13 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone. If the target is killed by this damage, it is absorbed into the mouther.
>
> ***Blinding Spittle (Recharge 4–6).*** The mouther spits a chemical glob at a point it can see within 30 feet of it. The glob explodes in a blinding flash of light on impact. Each creature within 10 feet of the flash must succeed on a DC 13 Dexterity saving throw or be blinded until the end of the mouther’s next turn.

\columnbreak

On a failure, the creature can’t take reactions until the start of its next turn and rolls a d8 to determine what it does during its turn. On a 1 to 4, the creature does nothing. On a 5 or 6, the creature takes no action or bonus action and uses all its movement to move in a randomly determined direction. On a 7 or 8, the creature makes a melee attack against a randomly determined creature within its reach or does nothing if it can’t make such an attack.

> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The gibbering mouther makes a bite attack and, if it can, uses its Blinding Spittle.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +8 to hit, reach 15 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 49 (9d10) piercing damage. If the target is Huge or smaller, it must succeed on a DC 16 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone. If the target is killed by this damage, it is absorbed into the mouther.
>
> ***Blinding Spittle (Recharge 3–6).*** The mouther spits a chemical glob at a point it can see within 45 feet of it. The glob explodes in a blinding flash of light on impact. Each creature within 20 feet of the flash must succeed on a DC 16 Dexterity saving throw or be blinded until the end of the mouther’s next turn.

>
> ***Aberrant Ground.*** The ground in a 20-foot radius around the mouther is doughlike difficult terrain. Each creature that starts its turn in that area must succeed on a DC 18 Strength saving throw or have its speed reduced to 0 until the start of its next turn.
>
> ***Gibbering.*** The mouther babbles incoherently while it can see any creature and isn’t incapacitated. Each creature that starts its turn within 40 feet of the mouther and can hear the gibbering must succeed on a DC 13 Wisdom saving throw. On a failure, the creature can’t take reactions until the start of its next turn and rolls a d8 to determine what it does during its turn. On a 1 to 4, the creature does nothing. On a 5 or 6, the creature takes no action or bonus action and uses all its movement to move in a randomly determined direction. On a 7 or 8, the creature makes a melee attack against a randomly determined creature within its reach or does nothing if it can’t make such an attack.

> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The gibbering mouther makes a bite attack and uses its Blinding Spittle.
>

> ### Legendary Actions
> 
> The  gibbering mouther can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The gibbering mouther regains spent legendary actions at the start of its turn.
> 
> ***Check.*** The gibbering mouther makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
>
> ***Flesh Tendril.*** The mouther sends a pseudopod at a Huge or smaller creature that just took its turn that the mouther can see within 60 feet of it. The creature must succeed on a DC 18 Dexterity saving throw or take 16 (3d10) bludgeoning damage and be grappled (escape DC 18). At the start of the mouther's turn, it can pull any creatures grappled this way 30 feet closer to it. 
>
> ***Maddening Whisper.*** The mouther whispers to a creature within 5 feet of it that can hear it that just took its turn. The creature must succeed on a DC 18 Wisdom saving throw or take 16 (3d10) psychic damage. It has disadvantage on this save if it is under the effect of the mouther's Gibbering ability
>
> ***Move.*** The gibbering mouther may move up to 15 without provoking attacks of opportunity.
> 
> ***Tenacious Will.*** If the gibbering mouther is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw as an action or at the beginning or end of its next turn, it may immediately make that save against the effect with advantage. It can use this legendary action while incapacitated.

### The Demon Wastes (Level 17-20)
**Activity Rating:** 1 Encounter per 3 Hrs. of Travel <br>
**Foraging DC:** 25 <br>
**Navigation DC:** 30 (Magical Aid Reduces It To 20) <br>
**Weather:** Save DCs for weather events range from 25-30.

The Demon Wastes, situated in the far north, teeters on the edge of a planar convergence with a demonic realm, imbuing the region with dark energies. This influence has twisted the landscape, turning it into a nightmarish wasteland. The area is plagued by frequent demonic incursions, with warmongering demons rampaging through, leaving destruction in their wake.

Driven by their infernal devotion, demon-worshipping barbarian tribes flock to the Demon Wastes, seeking to prove themselves to their demonic overlords. However, the land itself rebels against this desecration, unleashing aggressive elementals and supernatural wildlife to fiercely defend its sanctity. Anyone who dares intrude on these cursed lands risks facing not only the wrath of demons but also the vengeful fury of the land itself.

# Tundra <br> Creatures

## Bears 

 Bears are a symbol of strength and resilience, <br> captivating the imagination of humanoids across many cultures with their formidable presence and diverse range <br> of habitats. Known for their significant physical power, bears can take down large prey and defend themselves against most threats. Their thick fur and robust frames make them durable and allow them to withstand harsh conditions and engage in long pursuits.

Despite their substantial size, bears possess an unexpected speed and navigational versatility, enabling them to traverse challenging terrains, climb, and swim with remarkable proficiency. This agility complements their physical might, making them adept at catching swift prey or evading dangers in their natural habitats. Moreover, bears are equipped with keen senses, particularly an exceptional sense of smell, which aids them in tracking down food, sensing danger, and navigating their environment with an acute awareness.

Bears also display notable intelligence and problem-solving skills, especially when foraging for food or navigating obstacles.



\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br>

 This cognitive ability, combined with their capacity to learn from experiences, highlights their adaptability and interaction with their surroundings in innovative ways.

Adaptable to a wide range of environments, from arctic tundras to dense forests and mountainous regions, bears exemplify versatility and resilience. Their ability to thrive in various terrains speaks to their remarkable adaptability, ensuring their survival and prominence in the animal kingdom. The characteristics of bears, from their strength and agility to their intelligence and adaptability, make them awe-inspiring and deeply respected by those living in the wilder parts of the world.

The following are examples of different types of bears across a variety of sizes and power levels that can be found in boreal climates. Though it's not a comprehensive list of every type of bear, most other types could still be represented using the stat block of one of the bears presented here.

### Black Bears
Black bears, with their lustrous dark fur and imposing stature, wander the expansive wilds of their domain, a testament to their versatility and adaptability. These creatures are known to inhabit various enclaves of the wilderness, from deep, shadowed woods to the edges of vast and silent glades. While their fur is commonly as dark as night, some boast coats of cinnamon or even white, hinting at the rich diversity among their kind. This diversity is not merely cosmetic; it is a sign of a multitude of subspecies, each adapted to its unique corner of the natural world.

These bears are omnivorous, with a diet as varied as the lands they roam. They forage with an opportunistic zeal, partaking in nature's bounty from berry bush to honeycomb.

But, when the situation calls for it, they can hunt with a surprising combination of stealth and power.

Their keen intelligence and curiosity often lead them to explore and sometimes even manipulate their environments in search of sustenance or shelter.

In terms of demeanor, black bears are generally shy around other humanoids, often displaying a peaceful disposition. However, they possess a fierce protective instinct, especially when it comes to their offspring or when they are surprised and feel threatened, and in such cases, they can demonstrate the full force of their natural prowess. Their strength, coupled with sharp instincts, makes them respected by all who share their territory.

### Brown Bears
Brown bears are the stalwarts of the wilderness, with a range of fur colors that blend into the varied landscapes they inhabit. These large and powerful animals are found in numerous regions, each home to distinct subspecies with their own unique adaptations. Their diet is as broad as their habitat, consisting of fruits, nuts, fish, and small mammals, showcasing their omnivorous nature. 

While brown bears typically lead solitary lives, they may gather in numbers in areas of abundant food like a rich salmon run. They have a complex social structure that becomes apparent during these gatherings, where hierarchies are observed and occasionally contested. Despite their solitary nature, mothers are fiercely protective of their cubs, teaching them essential survival skills.

As winter approaches, brown bears enter a phase of intense eating known as hyperphagia to prepare for hibernation, significantly increasing their food intake to build fat reserves. This crucial period heightens their aggression as the drive to feed becomes paramount. Bears are more likely to encounter others during this time, defending their food sources fiercely. The necessity to fatten up can make them more dangerous, as they prioritize feeding over avoiding conflict, posing increased risks to themselves and others.

#### Grizzly Bears
The large and ferocious subspecies known as grizzly bears have captured the awe of those who share or venture into their territories. Their more aggressive nature is often a result of the fierce competition for resources and the need to defend their space. They are slightly larger than most other brown bears and have a distinct hump on their shoulders, a feature that highlights their powerful forelimbs and their ability to dig and forage. Grizzlies are particularly known for their impressive physical capabilities and can often be more aggressive and dangerous, especially when surprised or when they are with their cubs. Some grizzlies become brazen hunters, willing to attack humanoids without provocation. This has made them among the most feared animals by those traveling through remote wilds.

### Polar Bears

In the frigid expanses of the northern realms, the polar bear stands as a majestic and formidable hunter. These colossal beasts, robed in shimmering coats of snow-white fur, are the undisputed sovereigns of their icy domain. Adult males, towering and robust, can weigh as much as 700 kg, with females being notably smaller yet equally impressive.

Blessed with a thick layer of fat and a dense, water-repellent fur, these giants are insulated against the harshest of colds. Their bodies are so adept at retaining heat that the challenge often lies in staying cool rather than warm. With large, partially webbed front paws, Polar Bears are skilled swimmers, capable of traversing vast and treacherous waters. They are known to journey tirelessly across the seas, navigating the chilling waters with ease.

As apex predators, they primarily feast upon the seals that dwell in the same icy waters. They employ a cunning mix of patience and stealth, utilizing the sea ice as their hunting grounds to outwit their prey. Equipped with a remarkably acute sense of smell, polar bears can detect the faintest scent of a seal from a mile away, even under layers of snow and ice. Their vision and hearing, on par with humans, further enhance their hunting prowess. Should any humanoid adventurers venture into their icy domains, polar bears won't hesitate to employ the same hunting tactics against the unfortunate travelers. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

#### Tyrant Polar Bears
These primeval bears are larger and more robust than their 'modern' descendants. Thought to be extinct by most, some of these lone monsters still roam remote arctic wastelands where they hunt other large megafauna, spilling blood across the ice as they assert their rulership over this brutal domain. Tundra-dwelling humanoids may venerate these creatures as servants of the gods, and spiritual

<br>

> ##### New Condition: Dazed
> A dazed creature can’t take reactions and on its turn, it must choose whether it gets a move, an action, or a bonus action; it gets only one of the three.

### Arctotheriums

Arctotherium, the ancient primeval bear known as the short-faced bear, stands as a towering figure in the annals of natural history. These bears are characterized by their expansive chests and shortened snouts, a distinct feature from which they derive their name. Despite their formidable size, they are agile, capable of covering ground swiftly, a trait that serves them well in their pursuit of prey and sustenance.

These primeval creatures are omnivorous, with a preference for large meals to support their massive builds. Their diets are adaptable, consisting of anything the land offers, from vegetation to larger game. Arctotherium's powerful forelimbs and strong jaws are their primary tools, enabling them to hunt effectively and scavenge from others when the opportunity arises.

Arctotherium are typically solitary, with each bear maintaining a large territory that overlaps with others only occasionally. These territories are the stages upon which they silently enact their daily rituals of foraging, hunting, and roaming. Interaction between these ancient bears is rare, limited to necessary engagements such as mating or competing for resources.

Though often spoken of as relics of a bygone era, arctotheriums are still rumored to roam the remote and wild recesses of the world. They may be found deep in primeval forests, guarding ancient shrines dedicated to ursine gods, or in the service of powerful druids. Adventurers who stumble upon such beasts do well not to anger them, for the arctotheriums's power and ferocity is far beyond that of any other bear they will have faced.

### Ice Bears
These colossal creatures, resembling ordinary polar bears, are endowed with a mystical frost that seems to weave into their very being. Their fur, shimmering with a pale blue hue, glistens like the heart of a glacier, while their eyes gleam with the cold light of the aurora.

The origin of these majestic beasts is shrouded in mystery. Some say they are the children of the winter gods, blessed or cursed with their icy might. Others believe they are polar bears transformed by a powerful sorcery, their forms infused with the essence of the eternal frost. Regardless of their origins, their supernatural nature is unmistakable. 

The ice bears possess a remarkable ability to radiate an aura of frost, a chilling presence that seeps into the bones of any creature daring enough to come close. This aura not only slows down their prey, making escape difficult, but also serves as a shield, warding off those who might challenge these titans.

\columnbreak

<br><br>

In the heat of battle or when hunting, they can unleash a formidable wave of cold, a blast of freezing energy that envelops their surroundings. This wave can root their prey in place, encased in a sheath of ice, helpless against the might of the Ice Bear.

While these bears are known to hunt the typical fauna of their frozen homes, they have also earned a fearsome reputation for preying on humanoid hunters and frontiersmen who venture too far into their domain. Their attacks are swift and devastating, leaving little more than ice-covered remnants in their wake.

Despite their ferocity and mystical nature, there are tales of these mighty beasts being captured and tamed. In the hands of a skilled beastmaster, an Ice Bear can become a formidable beast of war, its natural abilities harnessed for battle. The sight of an armored Ice Bear charging into the fray, its breath frosting the air, is enough to shake the resolve of even the bravest warriors.

___
___
> ## Ice Bear
> *Large monstrosity, unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 14 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 168 (16d10 + 80)
> - **Speed** 40 ft., swim 25 ft.

>
> ***Aura of Frost.*** The bear has an aura of cold radiating from it in a 10-foot radius. Any creature that ends its turn within the aura must succeed on a DC 15 Constitution saving throw or its speed is halved until the end of its next turn, unless it is immune to cold damage.
>
> ***Keen Hearing and Smell.*** The bear has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on hearing and smell.
>
> ***Ice Walk.*** The bear can move across and climb icy surfaces without needing to make an ability check, and icy surfaces can't cause it to fall prone. Additionally, difficult terrain composed of ice or snow doesn't cost it extra movement.
>
> ***Snow Camouflage.*** The bear has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to hide in snowy terrain.
> 
> ### Actions
> ***Multiattack.*** The bear makes two attacks: one with its bite and one with its claws. It can use Ice Wave in place of its claw attack.
>

>

>
> ***Ice Wave (Recharges on a Short or Long Rest).*** A wave of encasing ice sweeps out from the bear in a 15-foot cube originating from it. The ground in the area is covered with slick ice, making it difficult terrain. A creature that moves into or within the area for the first time on its turn must succeed on a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw or fall prone. <br> Each creature in the cube, when it first appears, must make a DC 15 Strength saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 13 (3d8) cold damage and is restrained by ice for 1 minute. It or another creature within reach can use its action to make a DC 15 Strength check, shattering the ice on a success. The ice can also be attacked and destroyed (AC 15; 20 hp; vulnerability to fire, thunder, and bludgeoning damage; immunity to cold, poison, and psychic damage). On a successful save, a creature takes half as much damage and isn’t restrained.
>



\pagebreakNum


### Elemental Bears
These gargantuan elementals, born from the very essence of the arctic lands, take on the formidable forms of massive polar bears, embodying the raw, unbridled spirit of their frigid homelands.

With bodies sculpted from ice and snow, these majestic beings are more than mere animals; they are the personification of the arctic wilderness. Their fur seems to be made of frost and icicles, shimmering with the pale light of the winter sun. Their eyes, deep and piercing, reflect the endless skies of their frozen realms. These Elemental Bears do not just inhabit the Arctic; they are the Arctic, its protectors and avatars.

Their primary purpose is deeply ingrained in their icy souls – to guard their homelands from any threat. These guardians are fiercely territorial, confronting any who dare to disrupt the delicate balance of their icy domains. 

They are not just animals; they are the embodiment of the Arctic's will, its defenders against the encroachment of outsiders and the despoiling of their pristine landscapes.

Surrounded by an eternal maelstrom of winter winds, Elemental Bears command the very essence of cold and ice. They can breathe cones of icy hail, turning foes into frozen statues. With a roar that echoes across the tundra, they can unleash waves of ice from their massive bodies, capable of freezing everything in their path, creating landscapes of glacial beauty and deadly stillness.

#### The Avatar of Winter

Among these elemental titans, there exists a being of extraordinary power, known in whispered tales as the Avatar of Winter. This elemental bear is revered as a demi-god, a manifestation of the winter season itself. Larger, more powerful, and more ancient than its kin, the Avatar of Winter is a force of nature personified, capable of summoning blizzards and shaping the very ice at will.

> ### Legendary Actions
> The bear can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The bear regains spent legendary actions at the start of its turn.
> 
> **Check.** The bear makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
>
> **Claw of Ice.** The bear chooses a creature within 120 feet of it that just took its turn and is not restrained. That creature must succeed on a DC 20 Strength saving throw. On a failed save,  it is restrained by ice as by a claw of ice that forms around it. A creature can use its action to make a DC 20 Strength check, shattering the ice on a success. The ice can also be attacked and destroyed (AC 20; hp 20; vulnerability to fire, thunder, bludgeoning damage; immunity to cold, poison, and psychic damage). On a successful save, a creature isn't restrained.
>
> **Tenacious Will.** If the bear is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw as an action or at the beginning or end of its next turn, it may immediately make that save against the effect with advantage. It can use this legendary action while incapacitated.
>
> **Grasp of Winter** The bear chooses a creature within 120 feet of it that just took its turn and is restrained by ice, it is pulled 30 feet towards the bear or the center of its *soul of winter* spell if it is active (bear's choice).
>
> **Whirlwind of Frost (Costs 2 Actions).** The bear magically transforms into a whirlwind of ice, moves up to 60 feet, and reverts to its normal form. While in whirlwind form, the bear is immune to all damage and under the effects of the *gaseous form* spell. If it passes through another creature's space during this movement, that creature must succeed on a DC 20 Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, the target takes 14 (4d6) cold damage.

### Bear Tactics
Bears have very straightforward attack patterns that mostly involve charging straight at their prey. If they're not under the control of an external force, they will retreat when reduced to half health or lower or if it becomes obvious they are outmatched.

The supernatural bears have more complex tactics, as detailed below.

#### Ice Bear Tactics
Ice bears initiate combat by unleashing their ice wave ability and then targeting the physically weakest opponent restrained by the ice. If the ice bear isn't being controlled by another force, it will withdraw from combat if it fails to restrain any targets with its ice wave, or it loses half or more of its hit points within the first round.

#### Elemental Bear Tactics
Here are some things to keep in mind when using elemental bears:
* They are front-line fighters useful for tanking and crowd control
* Their Aura of Winter ability disrupts ranged attackers. So, elemental bears should try to close the distance with such enemies
* Ice Wave is its best opening move, followed by a bite attack on any restrained target
* Breath of Hail is a good follow-up move for the turn after Ice Wave is used since you can target everyone who's still restrained.
 * Breath of Hail is also useful for hitting foes who are staying out of range of Ice Wave if the bear can hit three or more enemies.
* Only use Frigid Bolt if there is no other way to attack enemies

#### Avatar of Winter Tactics
Here are some things to keep in mind when using the Avatar of Winter:
* The *soul of winter* spell is its best way of initiating combat, and it will cast it the most critical battlefield area as it isn't affected by the spell's adverse effects.
* The Claw of Ice with Grasp of Winter legendary actions can be used to pull targets back into the area of *soul of winter*.
* The Whirlwind of Frost action should be saved for situations where the bear is either unable to move or able to hit three or more enemies with it (assuming the bear ends up in a favorable location.)

<br>

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/GdNSd76/ursine-fylgja.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; left:-40px; width:570px;' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-580px;top:-20px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(100deg)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:75px; right:-20px; width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(0deg)' />

\pagebreakNum

### Bear Loot

The valuable items looted from bears will generally come from whatever can be harvested from them. This harvesting can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Nature)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest hide.

Being elementals, most of an elemental bear's form will disintegrate when it is destroyed. Players can loot the snow and dirt it leaves behind to find objects still holding some vestiges of its power. This can be done with an **Intelligence (Nature)** or **Wisdom (Nature)** check.

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Bear Loot Tables

If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

## Deer 
Existing across a vast range of environments in many forms, deer stand out as creatures of elegance, adaptability, and resilience. These graceful beings, ranging from the diminutive and sprightly to the majestic and formidable, embody a blend of agility, strength, and vigilance. 

Deer are also embodiments of agility and sensory acuity. Their lithe forms navigate the densest woods and roughest terrains with effortless grace. Keen senses — acute hearing and a robust sense of smell — keep them ever alert to potential threats, and their threats are many, for deer are often the favored prey of the many predators they share their homes with, from wolves to bears to humanoid hunters. 

Deer are such common prey that, for many humanoid cultures, they've come to be seen as symbols of the hunt. The stamina and endurance of these creatures are legendary. Capable of sustaining high-speed chases across vast distances, deer exhibit a remarkable blend of speed and endurance, qualities that have inspired countless tales and legends throughout the ages of great hunters pursuing particularly elusive deer.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

However, deer are far from helpless prey. Adorned with impressive antlers, a hallmark of their kind, the male deer (and some females, depending on species) exhibit a natural prowess in their horned charge. These antlers, far from mere ornaments of courtship, serve as formidable weapons in territorial disputes and self-defense. The deer's charge, a spectacular display of speed and strength, showcases their ability to confront challenges head-on.

Should deer find themselves retreating from attackers, they can utilize their hardened hoofs to deliver a powerful back-kick. This swift and unexpected maneuver enables them to fend off predators and threats even in retreat. The deer's muscular hind legs, engineered for both fleet-footed escapes and potent defense, make them creatures not to be underestimated.

The following are examples of different types of deer across a variety of sizes and power levels. Though it's not a comprehensive list of every type of deer, most other types could still be represented using the stat block of one of the deer presented here.

### Fallow Deer
These deer are as elegant as they are adaptable and grace many landscapes with their presence. Fallow deer can be identified by their impressive antlers and distinctive coats, which are particularly striking, exhibiting a range of colors from light tan with white mottling to dark chocolate brown and sometimes even pure white. The males boast large, unique antlers that are broad and shovel-like, a feature that distinguishes them from other deer species. These antlers are a significant part of their identity, shed and regrown annually.

Fallow deer often form herds, which can be quite large in areas with few natural predators or in protected environments. Their diet primarily consists of grasses, herbs, and leaves, with grazing typically occurring at dawn and dusk. During mating season, males engage in displays of strength and dominance to attract females. This involves intense vocalizations and physical confrontations, a dramatic display of natural behaviors.

\columnbreak

<br><br>

Fallow deer are skilled at adapting to various environments. Their ability to run swiftly and leap over obstacles serves them well in evading predators and navigating through different terrains. They are also vigilant and cautious, with keen senses that help them detect potential dangers, an essential aspect of their survival strategy.

In the realms they inhabit, fallow deer are admired for their beauty and the sense of tranquility they bring to their surroundings. Their grazing habits play a significant role in shaping the vegetation of their habitats, underlining their importance in the ecological balance of their ecosystems. Wilderness protectors such as druids and rangers ensure their numbers remain robust as they are vital to the health of their environment and provide an important food source to most large predators.

### Caribou
With their distinctive antlers and hardy nature, these animals epitomize the resilience and majesty of life in the harsh northern climates. Caribou are large deer, notable for both males and females possessing antlers, a unique trait among deer species. These antlers are grand and intricate, used for foraging in the snow and as a display during mating seasons. The coat of a caribou is dense and weather-resistant, varying in color but typically exhibiting shades of brown, gray, and white, providing excellent insulation and camouflage in their natural habitats.

Socially, caribou are known for their migratory habits, often traveling in large herds across vast distances. This migration is a spectacular sight and is driven by their search for food, mating opportunities, and calving grounds. Caribou diets are versatile, feeding on a variety of vegetation, including lichens, known as reindeer moss, grasses, and leaves, adapting their diet to the changing seasons.

The breeding season for caribou is a time of heightened activity. Males compete for females through displays of antler size and strength. They generally only give birth to a single calf at a time, and these calves grow quickly, a necessity for survival in the often harsh conditions of their habitats.

In terms of survival strategies, caribou are well-equipped for life in the challenging north. Their large, wide hooves are adapted for walking on snow and soft ground, acting like natural snowshoes. They are also excellent swimmers, an ability that aids them in crossing large rivers and lakes during their migrations.

Caribou play a significant role in their ecosystems. Their migration patterns and grazing habits have profound effects on the vegetation and overall health of the landscapes they traverse. Many northern tribes and civilizations use caribou as herd animals that are vital to their survival in the resource scarce north. As such, caribou come to hold major cultural significance and are featured in many legends and folktales of these peoples.

### Elk 
Known for their impressive stature and striking antlers, elk are among the largest species of deer, with males significantly larger than females. They are distinguished by their impressive antlers, which are some of the largest of any deer species, with a complex, branching structure. These antlers, shed annually, are not just a symbol of their strength but also play a crucial role during the mating season. The elk's thick coat changes from a light tan in summer to a darker brown in winter, providing  camouflage and insulation.

Elk are known for their herd behavior. While females and young typically form large herds, males may either join these herds or form smaller groups of their own. These herds are dynamic and can change in size and composition with the seasons. Elks' diet is predominantly grass-based, but they also feed on leaves, bark, and shrubs, showing adaptability in their feeding habits to suit the environment.



___

> *Large beast, unaligned*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 12
> - **Hit Points** 19 (3d10 + 3)
> - **Speed** 50 ft.

\columnbreak

During mating season, bulls engage in dramatic displays of strength and dominance to attract mates, including bugling, a loud series of vocalizations, and displaying their antlers. Calves are born with spotted coats for camouflage, a critical survival trait in their early days.

Survival for elk involves a blend of physical prowess and keen instincts. Their large size and strength are their primary defenses against predators. Additionally, their acute hearing and sense of smell enable them to detect danger early. These senses, combined with their speed and power, allow them to fight or flee depending on the threat they face.

In the various realms they inhabit, elk are revered for their beauty and strength. Their majestic presence and mighty antlers make them a prized game for hunters, and many grand hunts focus center on the pursuit of a majestic elk. Creatures tied to the fey wild, such as elves, sometimes utilize elk as swift and powerful mounts, allowing them to gracefully bound through the wilds before crashing into foes with the antlers of their wild steed.

### Moose
The moose is the largest and most imposing of the <br> modern deer. With their towering stature and <br> distinctive antlers, moose command an imposing <br> presence in the landscapes they inhabit.

Moose are remarkable for their size, with males <br> being significantly larger than females. One of the <br> most striking features of the moose is its antlers, <br> which are the largest of any deer species. These <br> antlers, exclusive to males, spread impressively <br> wide and are shed annually. The moose's coat, thick <br> and coarse, varies in color from brown to black, <br> offering insulation against the cold climates they <br> often inhabit.

Moose are mostly solitary, except during the <br> mating season or when mothers are raising their <br> young. They wander alone through vast northern <br> territories, relying on their size rather than a herd <br> to protect them from predators. Moose are <br> herbivores, feeding on a diet rich in both aquatic <br> and terrestrial vegetation, including leaves, bark, <br> pine cones, twigs, and shoots. 

During mating season, male moose engage in <br> fierce competitions for the attention of females, <br> often involving physical displays and antler clashes. <br> Their calves grow rapidly, as size is a necessary <br> part of their survival strategy against the harsh <br> conditions and fierce predators they must endure.

Once they are fully grown, moose can rely on <br> their size and strength to fend off threats. Their <br> large antlers serve as a deterrent to predators, <br> and their long legs are capable of powerful kicks. <br> Moose are also excellent swimmers, an ability that <br> aids them in foraging for aquatic plants and <br> escaping predators.

As some of the most imposing creatures of their <br> northern habits, moose are often utlized as prized <br> guardians and steeds by druids. Moose are typically <br> not trainable by mundane means, and only those <br> with a supernatural connection to the wild can hope <br> to leverage their mighty.

\columnbreak

### Megaloceros
These primeval deer dwell in remote time-lost tundras alongside other ancient megafauna. Megaloceros are one of the largest deer species to have ever lived, with males displaying a remarkable set of antlers, some of the largest in any deer species, both in width and length. These antlers, which can span up to 12 feet from tip to tip, are not only a display of dominance but a tool used in mating rituals and defense against predators. Their robust and muscular bodies are covered in a thick coat of fur that varies in color, aiding them in adapting to colder climates.

The social and breeding behaviors of the megaloceros are similar to those of other deer, with males vying with each other during mating season. The males use their impressive antlers to gain the attention of females and to establish dominance within their herds. These antlers also serve as a menecing warning to any who would threaten the herd.

Survival for megaloceros, given their size and habitat, involves a blend of sheer physical presence, speed, and honed senses. Their large antlers, while majestic, can present navigational challenges, particularly in maneuvering dense forests. As a result, megaloceros prefer to roam open grassy landscapes where they can leverage their size and speed. 

\columnbreak
