### Werewolverines
Few lycanthropes exhibit the savagery and fearlessness seen in werewolverines, and victims of their curse become battle-hungry seekers of bloody combat. Even the two natural weaknesses of werewolverines, silver and fire, cannot deter them when they are consumed by the frenzy of their curse.

***Warrior Nomads.*** Most werewolverines are solitary by nature, roaming frigid tundras or remote mountains alone. However, they possess an insatiable desire to confront the most formidable opponents they can find, traveling great distances from one fight to the next and leaving a trail of bloodshed in their wake. Legends from these frozen lands tell of werewolverines appearing before villages and tribes, demanding challenges from their mightiest warriors. 

These creatures often terrorize the communities, extorting food and treasure before moving on. When a werewolverine encounters a worthy adversary within a community, it may bite them, spreading its curse. The bitten individual is allowed to live but is marked for future confrontation, with the hope that they may one day provide a worthy challenge.

***Lycanthrope Hunters.*** Werewolverines pose a special threat to other lycanthropes they encounter. Werewolverines often carry silver-tipped javelins, as they view werewolves, werebears, and even other werewolverines as truly worthy kills. Most other lycanthropes consider werewolverines to be deranged and avoid them at all costs, even relinquishing territory and resources to appease these fearsome creatures. 

\columnbreak

___
___
> ## Werewolverine
> *Medium humanoid (human, shapechanger), chaotic neutral*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 13 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 93 (11d8 + 44)
> - **Speed** 30 ft., (30 ft., climb 20 ft., burrow 5 ft. in wolverine or hybrid form)
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|16 (+3)|14 (+2)|18 (+4)|10 (+0)|14 (+2)|12 (+1)|
>___
> - **Skills** Athletics +5, Intimidation +6, Perception +4
> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 14
> - **Languages** Common (can't speak in wolverine form)
> - **Challenge** 4 (1,100 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +2
> ___
> ***Implacable.*** The werewolverine has advantage on saving throws against being charmed, frightened, stunned, paralyzed, or incapacitated.
>
> ***Keen Smell.*** The werewolverine has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell.
>
> ***Reckless.*** At the start of its turn, the werewolverine can gain advantage on all melee weapon attack rolls during that turn, but attack rolls against it have advantage until the start of its next turn.
>
> ***Regeneration.*** The werewolverine regains 10 hit points at the start of its turn. If the werewolverine takes fire damage or damage from a silvered weapon, this trait doesn't function at the start of the werewolverine's next turn. The werewolverine dies only if it starts its turn with 0 hit points and doesn't regenerate.
>
> ***Stench (Wolverine or Hybrid Form Only).*** Any creature other than a werewolverine that starts its turn within 5 feet of the werewolverine must succeed on a DC 14 Constitution saving throw or be poisoned until the start of the creature's next turn. On a successful saving throw, the creature is immune to the stench of all werewolverines for 1 hour.
> 
> ### Actions
> ***Multiattack.*** The werewolverine makes two attacks, only one of which can be with its bite.
>
> ***Bite (Wolverine or Hybrid Form Only).*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 11 (2d8 + 3) piercing damage. If the target is a humanoid, it must succeed on a DC 14 Constitution saving throw or be cursed with werewolverine lycanthropy.
>
> ***Claws (Wolverine or Hybrid Form Only).*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 9 (1d12 + 3) slashing damage.
>
> ***Javelin (Humanoid or Hybrid Form Only).*** *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 30/120 ft., one target. *Hit:* 6 (1d6 + 3) piercing damage.
> 
> ### Bonus Actions
> ***Shapechanger.*** The werewolverine can use its action to polymorph into a wolverine-humanoid hybrid or into a wolverine, or back into its true form, which is humanoid. Its statistics are the same in each form. Any equipment it is wearing or carrying isn’t transformed. It reverts to its true form if it dies.

### Burning Rage Wolverines
In the frozen expanses of the world, where massive beasts roam amidst icy tundras, one creature instills fear even in these formidable inhabitants—the burning rage Wolverine. This creature takes the form of a massive wolverine, engulfed in noxious flames that reek of sulfur. Its claws blaze with heated brimstone, causing the ice and snow beneath its paws to melt away.

***Ice Hunters.*** The fiery claws and teeth of the Burning Rage Wolverine make it a perfect hunter of the large ice beasts and creatures that dwell in the cold corners of the world. These creatures rely on these hunts to sustain their supernatural flames. Among their prey are ice caribou, yetis, frost salamanders, and occasionally, even frost wurms and young tundra-dwelling dragons have fallen victim to their relentless appetite. Their affinity for icey creatures even drives them to hunt wizards and druids who wield ice magic. 

***Charred Homes.*** Beyond their fiery claws, they possess the ability to release waves of scorching stench that can overwhelm creatures adapted to colder climates. This noxious stench can be launched over great distances in explosive bursts, poisoning and burning their unfortunate victims.

When a burning rage wolverines successfully bring down particularly massive prey, they carve out the creature's body and repurpose it into a new dwelling. These repurposed corpses serve as shelter, keeping them warm and sustaining them through the harshest winter seasons. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Sometimes, they also serve as a home for a mating pair to give birth to their young. Adventurers should exercise caution if they come across a charred corpse in the midst of the tundra, as burning rage wolverines are fiercely territorial and will not tolerate any intruders near their abodes.

___
___
> ## Burning Rage Wolverine
> *Large elemental, chaotic neutral*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 16 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 157 (15d10 + 75)
> - **Speed** 30 ft., climb 20 ft., burrow 10 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|20 (+5)|12 (+1)|20 (+5)|5 (-3)|14 (+2)|10 (+0)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Int +1
> - **Damage Immunities** cold, fire
> - **Skills** Intimidation +8, Perception +6
> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., tremorsense 30 ft., passive Perception 16
> - **Languages** None 
> - **Challenge** 9 (5,000 XP) &emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +4
> ___
>
> ***Choking Smog.*** Any creature that starts its turn within 10 feet of the one more creatures with this ability must succeed on a DC 17 Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, the creature takes 7 (2d6) fire damage and is poisoned until the start of the creature's next turn. On a successful save, the creature takes half as much damage and isn't poisoned. If the creature fails the save by 5 or more (DC 12), the creature is stunned until the poison ends. A creature that has resistance to fire damage has advantage on the saving throw, and a creature that is immune to fire damage automatically succeeds. A creature that has vulnerability to fire damage has disadvantage on the saving throw.
>
> ***Implacable.*** The wolverine has advantage on saving throws against being charmed, frightened, stunned, paralyzed, or incapacitated.
>
> ***Keen Smell.*** The wolverine has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell.
>
> ***Reckless.*** At the start of its turn, the wolverine can gain advantage on all melee weapon attack rolls during that turn, but attack rolls against it have advantage until the start of its next turn.
> 
> ### Actions
> ***Multiattack.*** The wolverine makes three attacks: one with its bite and two with its claws.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 16 (2d10 + 5) piercing damage plus 13 (2d12) fire damage.
>
> ***Claws.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit:* 10 (1d10 + 5) slashing damage plus 6 (1d12) fire damage.
>
> ***Sulfur Spray (Recharges on a Short or Long Rest).*** The wolverine releases a spray of burning fumes from its rear in a 30-foot cone. Each creature in that area must make a DC 17 Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 14 (4d6) poison damage and 14 (4d6) fire damage and is covered in the toxic spray for the next minute. On a success, a creature takes half as much damage and isn't covered in spray. Until a creature uses its action to scrape or wash the spray off itself or another creature, it has the wolverine's Choking Smog ability (the creature is subjected to its own Choking Smog at the start of each of its turns).

> ## Burning Rage Wolverine Alpha
> If you want your burning rage wolverine to be suitable for solo encounters against the players by itself, you can increase its hit points to 204 (24d10+72) and give it the legendary actions described below. Doing so increases its CR to 13.
>
> ### Legendary Actions
> The wolverine can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The wolverine regains spent legendary actions at the start of its turn.
> 
> **Check.** The wolverine makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
> 
> **Move.** The wolverine moves up to 15 feet without provoking attacks of opportunity.
>
> **Slash.** The wolverine makes a *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. Hit: 7 (1d4 + 5) slashing damage plus 6 (1d12) fire damage. If the wolverine used its Reckless feature on its last turn, it has advantage on the attack roll.
>
> **Tenacious Will.** If the wolverine is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw as an action or at the beginning or end of its next turn, it may immediately make that save against the effect with advantage. It can use this legendary action while incapacitated.
>
> **Recharge. (Costs 2 Actions)** The wolverine recharges its Sulfur Spray ability.

### Wolverine Adventures
The following table provides some ways to create adventures that utilize these ferocious beasts:

##### Wolverine Adventure Hooks 

| d12  | Adventure Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Wolverine Beacon:** The adventurers join an expedition to the frozen north, where they must survive encounters with aggressive wolverines while searching for an artifact said to attract the creatures and drive them to heightened levels of aggression.|
|  2  | **The Snarling Caverns:** An ancient druidic treasure is rumored to be hidden in a cave system known as the Snarling Caverns, a dangerous place filled with traps and inhabited by a pack of unusually intelligent wolverines left by the former druidic inhabitants.|
|  3  |**Wolverine Wranglers:** A nature warden enlists the adventurers' help in relocating several wolverines that have wandered into a populated area. The mission requires careful planning and non-lethal methods to safely move the animals back to their natural habitat. |



\columnbreak



|   |  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  4  | **Primeval Spirits:** The players come across a small town haunted by spirits believed to be the echoes of ancient megalictises that roamed the area in ages past. Superstitious locals think the spirits of these "dire wolverines" are returning in the flesh to hunt the intruders in their territory.   |
|  5  | **The Scorched Tundra:** The adventurers stumble upon a tundra that has been scorched and melted, with local wildlife devastated. The cause is a Burning Rage Wolverine, which must be tracked and dealt with before it turns the entire region into a wasteland. |
|  6  | **The Ice Mage's Request:** An ice mage seeks a component found only within the body of a Burning Rage Wolverine for a powerful spell to counter a growing fire elemental threat. The adventurers are hired to hunt one of these creatures and retrieve the needed component.|
|  7  | **The Charred Den:** While traveling through a harsh tundra, the players find the charred corpse of a frost worm, which they have either been tasked with harvesting or must take shelter in to avoid an incoming storm. However, they soon find themselves facing the fiery elemental wolverine dwelling within. |
|  8  | **Icy Vengence:** The players encounter an adult tundra-dwelling dragon (either a savage white dragon or benevolent silver dragon) whose younger kin have been slain by a burning rage wolverine. The dragon offers them a reward in exchange for helping it enact its revenge.|
|  9  |**The Nomad's Trail:** The adventurers must track a werewolverine across the tundra, following a trail of destruction. Their journey leads them through harsh environments, facing the creature’s previous victims and other dangers of the wild. |
|  10  | **The Lycanthrope Hunter:** A werebear whose kin have been slain by a brutal werewolverine hunter approaches the players, asking them for help in putting a stop to the killer before he becomes the next victim. |
|  11  | **The Werewolverine's Arena:** A ruthless lord has captured a werewolverine and is using it as the star attraction in his gladiatorial games. The adventurers can be captured and forced to fight, tasked with rescuing the creature, or hired to stop the games altogether. However, they may soon find the werewolverine is all too happy to remain and enjoy the neverending bloodshed.|
|  12  | **Curse of Fury:** One of the adventurers or a key NPC has been bitten by a werewolverine and is now marked for a future confrontation. The party must seek a cure for the curse or prepare for the inevitable battle when the werewolverine returns.|

\pagebreakNum



### Wolverine Tactics
Wolverines rely on sheer ferocity to defeat their opponents and aren't afraid to confront creatures that are larger or tougher, especially if there's a potential meal at stake. In one-on-one combat, wolverines always employ their reckless attack feature. However, when facing multiple foes, they opt not to use this feature.

#### Burning Rage Wolverines Tactics:
These elementals generally employ the same tactics as regular wolverines. However, when faced with overwhelming numbers, they may initiate the encounter with their Sulfur Spray to even the odds.


**Burning Rage Wolverine Alpha Tactics.**
This variant utilizes its legendary move actions to close the distance with opponents. Once in range, it relies on its Slash legendary action to initiate melee combat. If its opponents prove to be evasive or are out of reach, the alpha will prioritize recharging its Sulfur Spray ability.

#### Werewolverine Tactics

Werewolverines are typically solitary creatures, although they may occasionally have a few underlings whom they've coerced into serving them. These lycanthropes tend to adopt the tactics of their namesake, the wolverine (described above). 

In combat, they focus their ferocity on a single target, usually one they deem worthy of carrying their curse. They rely on their claws and avoid using their bite attack until the targeted individual reaches half health or two rounds have passed without the opponent dying or being rendered unconscious. This delay signifies the werewolverine's recognition of the target's worthiness to bear its curse.

\columnbreak

### Wolverine Loot
The valuable items looted from wolverines will generally come from whatever can be harvested from them. This harvesting can usually be done using a **Wisdom (Survival)** or **Intelligence (Nature)** check. However, you may allow players proficient with specific tools to harvest items related to that tool. For example, a character might make a Wisdom (Leathworker’s Tools) check to harvest hide.

Being elementals, most of a burning rage wolverine's form will disintegrate when it is destroyed. Players can loot the burnt stone and ashes it leaves behind to find objects still holding some vestiges of its power. This can be done with an **Intelligence (Nature)** or **Wisdom (Nature)** check.

Because lycanthropes revert to their humanoid form when they are slain, most of the valuable items players can collect from werewolverines will be worn items or items dropped by their former victims. These valuables may include standard coinage. These items can be found using a **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** check.

Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Wolverine Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

|:---:|:-----------:|

|  8-17 | 1 1gp Item | 
|  18+ | 1 2gp Item  |

## Yule Cats
Stalking villages in harsh winter environments, the yule cat strikes terror into the hearts of those who would skirt their responsibilities near the holiday season. The monster appears to be a typical fluffy cat, except it is roughly the size of a polar bear. Its yellow eyes glow with fiendish malice, betraying its unnatural origin, and its teeth and claws are capable of ripping through villagers with ease. 

***Hunters of the Indolent.*** Yule cats primarily stalk towns in cold, harsh environments, usually as significant holiday events approach. The yule cat will look for villagers with a specific identifier that indicates they have shirked their duties that year. The most common identifier is someone lacking new clothes, as this implies the individual didn't adequately aid the community in preparing clothes for the coming winter. 

However, these identifiers can vary depending on the traditions and economic exports of the village. In a town known for crafting and trading jewelry to survive, the yule cat may instead target villagers without any form of newly crafted jewelry on their person. Whatever the indicator, the yule cat will ruthlessly hunt and kill these individuals, whether men, women, or children.

***Winter Stalkers of Unknown Origin.***
While yule cats are fiendish in nature, their origins are not wholly known. Some claim they are the pets of mountain-dwelling hags and giants sent to torment lazy humanoids. Others believe them to be divine punishment resulting from villagers not doing their part to help the community in times of hardship.

Regardless of their origin, yule cats invariably roam wintery environments using feline hunting methods to prey upon their targeted villagers. Despite their large size, yule cats can easily blend into snowy landscapes, even hiding within snow flurries with supernatural ease. Victims will often be within pouncing range before they notice the fiend, even while within the supposed safety of their village.  

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

If a yule cat's victim notices it and attempts to escape, the fiend can freeze its target in place with a dreadful glare.  Once its prey is paralyzed, the yule cat will take its time tormenting and playing with its soon-to-be meal.  Some yule cats will even allow their prey the illusion of escape just before making the killing strike.

##### Yule Cat Adventurers
| d6  | Adventure Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | A town's citizens have become indolent, falling behind on producing needed clothes for the coming winter.  A town elder has summoned the yule cat to teach the population a harsh lesson.|
|  2  | A hag gives out clothes to poor children living in rags.  The children who refuse her gifts and continue wearing their rags are hunted by her pet yule cat.   |
|  3  | A sadistic and fashion-obsessed bard has gained control of a yule cat.  Townsfolk who fail to keep up with the latest clothing trends are hunted by the beast. |
|  4  | A yule cat is the favored pet of a vain cloud giant who lords over a dwarven mining village.  Dwarves who don't adorn themselves with newly mined gems each year are hunted by the cat.  |
|  5  |A village regularly wracked by storms must repair its homes each year.  The yule cat destroys any home left in disrepair and devours its inhabitants.  |
|  6  | A toymaker has devised a way to ensure his employees stay focused on making enough goods for the coming holiday: workers who fail to meet their quotas are hunted by a yule cat. |

> ## Yule Cat
>*Large fiend, neutral evil*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 15 (natural armor)
> - **Hit Points** 200 (16d12+96)
> - **Speed** 50 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|22 (+6)|18 (+4)|20 (+5)|14 (+2)|18 (+4)|16 (+3)|
>___
> - **Saving Throws** Dex +7, Con +8
> - **Skills** Investigation +5, Perception +7,  Stealth +7, Survival +7 
> - **Damage Resistances** cold
> - **Senses** darkvision 120 ft., passive Perception 17
> - **Languages** understands Giant, Infernal, and Sylvan but can't speak
> - **Challenge** 8 (3,900 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp;&emsp;  **Proficiency Bonus** +3    
> ___
>
> ***Keen Sight.*** The yule cat has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on sight.
>
> ***Holiday Clothing.*** The yule cat treats creatures wearing new clothing they've received within the last month as though they are under the effects of the *protection from evil and good* spell.
>
> ***Pounce.*** If the yule cat jumps at least 10 feet straight towards a creature and then hits it with a claw attack on the same turn, the target must succeed on a DC 17 Strength saving throw or be knocked prone.
>
> ***Snow Stalker.*** The yule cat has advantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks made to hide in snowy terrain and can do so even if it is only lightly obscured while in such terrain.
>
> ***Snow Strider.*** The yule cat ignores difficult terrain and slipping hazards caused by ice and snow.
>
> ### Actions
> ***Multiattack.*** The yule cat makes two attacks: one with its bite and one with its claws. If both attacks hit the same target, the target is grappled (escape DC 17). Until this grapple ends, the yule cat can't attack another target.
>
> ***Bite.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 24 (4d8 + 6) piercing damage.  If the target is prone, it takes 42 (8d8 + 6) piercing damage instead.
>
> ***Claw.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +9 to hit, reach 5 ft., one target. *Hit*: 19 (2d12 + 6) slashing damage.
>
> ***Winter's Gaze.*** The yule cat targets one creature it can see within 100 feet of it. The target must succeed on a DC 15 Constitution saving throw or be paralyzed for 1 minute unless it is wearing new clothing it received within the last month. The target can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success. If the target's saving throw is successful, or if the effect ends on it, the target is immune to the Winter's Gaze of all yule cats for 1 hour.

> ##### Beyond Simple Clothing
> The Holiday Clothing and Winter's Gaze features are built around the assumption you are running a traditional Yule Cat from Islandic folklore that hunts individuals based on their clothing.  This legend is likely rooted in the fact that clothing production was a vital aspect of daily life for the Islandic villages where this tale originated.  You can modify these abilities to focus on a different feature that better suits the primary industry or customs of the town being terrified by the yule cat.  The primary theme of the yule cat is that it hunts those who have not done their part for the village.  You can adapt it to identify these individuals in a way that makes the most sense for your setting.
